id="viewport" data-kaios-focus-transparent="1"><h1 style="display:block;height:0;overflow:hidden;position:absolute;width:0;padding:0">Facebook</h1><div id="page"><div class="_129_" id="header-notices"></div><div class="_59e9" id="root" role="main" data-sigil="context-layer-root content-pane"><div class="_7om2 _4ft8"><div class="_4g34"><!-- begin-react-placeholder --><div><div id="u_0_1_9s"><noscript id="u_0_2_OO"></noscript><div class="_11u6"><a href="/communitystandards/?video"><i class="img img _2sxw _4s0y" style="background-image: url(&#039;https\3a //static.xx.fbcdn.net/rsrc.php/v3/yr/r/WhZnYf_tjgg.png&#039;);background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:100% 100%;-webkit-background-size:100% 100%;padding-bottom:56.25%;"></i></a></div><div class="_12bc _11wv"><div><div class="_297a"><div class="_21c0"><div class="_21c1">INTRODUCTION</div><div class="_4n96"><p class="_3i--">Every day, people use Facebook to share their experiences, connect with friends and family, and build communities. We are a service for more than two billion people to freely express themselves across countries and cultures and in dozens of languages.</p><p class="_3i--">We recognize how important it is for Facebook to be a place where people feel empowered to communicate, and we take seriously our role in keeping abuse off our service. That’s why we’ve <a href="https://lm.facebook.com/l.php?u=https%3A%2F%2Fnewsroom.fb.com%2Fnews%2F2019%2F04%2Finsidefeed-community-standards-development-process%2F&amp;h=AT1-SJMwPbzyR1aFB__Mj0RLL7HT6R1kY1eSft0gKKInSRpoWRfpq4Hu16hS4kkXHRUWOn8q9IH_zVixORvFInl1Jry8PQVCrDBq8ZKhX80KYdoOaBJ73SL1h3Se_WfeSgIHimAg4zjlvn3kEKK8CXaXRJvYn7UHLmsf" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" data-lynx-mode="asynclazy">developed a set of Community Standards</a> that outline what is and is not allowed on Facebook. Our policies are based on feedback from our community and the advice of experts in fields such as technology, public safety and human rights. To ensure that everyone’s voice is valued, we take great care to craft policies that are inclusive of different views and beliefs, in particular those of people and communities that might otherwise be overlooked or marginalized.</p><div style="text-align: center"><i class="img _257 _4cef img _2sxw" style="background-image: url(&#039;https\3a //scontent-sea1-1.xx.fbcdn.net/v/t39.2365-6/30179729_1969747913355382_7724706176021037056_n.png?_nc_cat\3d 1\26 ccb\3d 1-3\26 _nc_sid\3d ad8a9d\26 _nc_ohc\3d -RhxVcwFZXwAX_qDlEO\26 _nc_ht\3d scontent-sea1-1.xx\26 oh\3d 5e5edac8eb31a5b6972ae81090d11285\26 oe\3d 6088DCFA&#039;);background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:100% 100%;-webkit-background-size:100% 100%;width:166px;height:163px;"></i></div><br /><div class="_21c1">REITERATING OUR COMMITMENT TO VOICE</div><p class="_3i--">The goal of our Community Standards has always been to <a href="https://lm.facebook.com/l.php?u=https%3A%2F%2Fnewsroom.fb.com%2Fnews%2F2018%2F08%2Fhard-questions-free-expression%2F&amp;h=AT0FWQhPDA5BJFljoIpr7IUh2eLBog5fvFAoLml0-MkxcyJWkJUWQkZjF85YRF2V7-3fPi9GJRlSxwyUeP-OGpOsxbo6jU3aqQIis-mHwMzMDFK3sLtXlYZo61w8Kg8LddYaYhquqG3T5o-uWiyoKoi8itl81ovzss-H" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" data-lynx-mode="asynclazy">create a place for expression and give people a voice</a>. This has not and will not change. Building community and bringing the world closer together depends on people’s ability to share diverse views, experiences, ideas and information. We want people to be able to talk openly about the issues that matter to them, even if some may disagree or find them objectionable. In some cases, we allow content for public awareness which would otherwise go against our Community Standards – if it is newsworthy and in the public interest. We do this only after weighing the public interest value against the risk of harm and we look to international human rights standards,<a href="https://lm.facebook.com/l.php?u=https%3A%2F%2Fabout.fb.com%2Fwp-content%2Fuploads%2F2021%2F03%2FFacebooks-Corporate-Human-Rights-Policy.pdf&amp;h=AT28zP7S1srRLbV3gMPyyoqWWC5VePR--nTSPy78oIBUMVj4So-xc6vw8E4Uv5Gu6DrTMDZrFiOmm4956Jiq0CwVLJu2cxSBwZcl8yK19vumRV109EgNRhM7iskNKKeTYx8agOJCWbJQdWcfMay1yTDHopRDoGhvff-w" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" data-lynx-mode="asynclazy"> as reflected in our Corporate Human Rights Policy,</a> to make these judgments. As such, we consider the newsworthiness of content posted by anyone, including news organizations and individuals users. For example, we have allowed content that graphically depicts war or the consequences of war where it is important to public discourse.</p><p class="_3i--">Our commitment to expression is paramount, but we recognize the internet creates new and increased opportunities for abuse. For these reasons, when we limit expression, we do it in service of one or more of the following values:</p><br /><div style="text-align: center"><i class="img _257 _4cef img _2sxw" style="background-image: url(&#039;https\3a //scontent-sea1-1.xx.fbcdn.net/v/t39.2365-6/70546071_460725341450782_7389006442629431296_n.png?_nc_cat\3d 1\26 ccb\3d 1-3\26 _nc_sid\3d ad8a9d\26 _nc_ohc\3d OPMPY95-B2MAX-81wQk\26 _nc_ht\3d scontent-sea1-1.xx\26 oh\3d d773106736adfa2f5fc3b5969b3d513e\26 oe\3d 6089E925&#039;);background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:100% 100%;-webkit-background-size:100% 100%;width:172px;height:162px;"></i></div><p class="_3i--"><b>Authenticity:</b> We want to make sure the content people are seeing on Facebook is authentic. We believe that authenticity creates a better environment for sharing, and that’s why we don’t want people using Facebook to misrepresent who they are or what they’re doing. </p><div style="text-align: center"><i class="img _257 _4cef img _2sxw" style="background-image: url(&#039;https\3a //scontent-sea1-1.xx.fbcdn.net/v/t39.2365-6/30179798_233411330550983_830803110640222208_n.png?_nc_cat\3d 1\26 ccb\3d 1-3\26 _nc_sid\3d ad8a9d\26 _nc_ohc\3d yOk0jgmX8d0AX9c4M-R\26 _nc_ht\3d scontent-sea1-1.xx\26 oh\3d 3ee60ff16715a3ae5c910dcb471fbfac\26 oe\3d 60891063&#039;);background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:100% 100%;-webkit-background-size:100% 100%;width:166px;height:163px;"></i></div><p class="_3i--"><b>Safety:</b> We are committed to making Facebook a safe place. Expression that threatens people has the potential to intimidate, exclude or silence others and isn’t allowed on Facebook.</p><br /><div style="text-align: center"><i class="img _257 _4cef img _2sxw" style="background-image: url(&#039;https\3a //scontent-sea1-1.xx.fbcdn.net/v/t39.2365-6/70744027_1120870694776290_6189555203662938112_n.png?_nc_cat\3d 1\26 ccb\3d 1-3\26 _nc_sid\3d ad8a9d\26 _nc_ohc\3d DTqZS0zSAv4AX-JVTtu\26 _nc_ht\3d scontent-sea1-1.xx\26 oh\3d 2e201a669802394858f63544df91e6e1\26 oe\3d 6089EFD0&#039;);background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:100% 100%;-webkit-background-size:100% 100%;width:172px;height:162px;"></i></div><p class="_3i--"><b>Privacy:</b> We are committed to protecting personal privacy and information. Privacy gives people the freedom to be themselves, and to choose how and when to share on Facebook and to connect more easily. </p><div style="text-align: center"><i class="img _257 _4cef img _2sxw" style="background-image: url(&#039;https\3a //scontent-sea1-1.xx.fbcdn.net/v/t39.2365-6/70707979_539090683561979_6815354865225564160_n.png?_nc_cat\3d 1\26 ccb\3d 1-3\26 _nc_sid\3d ad8a9d\26 _nc_ohc\3d AdhWdWqp4S4AX-eRLU-\26 _nc_ht\3d scontent-sea1-1.xx\26 oh\3d 896db37bd0628e4f1226e80bce0b5d32\26 oe\3d 608768C2&#039;);background-repeat:no-repeat;background-size:100% 100%;-webkit-background-size:100% 100%;width:159px;height:167px;"></i></div><p class="_3i--"><b>Dignity:</b> We believe that all people are equal in dignity and rights. We expect that people will respect the dignity of others and not harass or degrade others.</p><p class="_3i--">Our Community Standards apply to everyone, all around the world, and to all types of content. They’re designed to be comprehensive – for example, content that might not be considered hateful may still be removed for violating a different policy. We recognize that words mean different things or affect people differently depending on their local community, language, or background. We work hard to account for these nuances while also applying our policies consistently and fairly to people and their expression. Our enforcement of these standards relies on information available to us. In some cases, this means that we may not detect content and behavior that violates these standards, and in others, <a href="https://lm.facebook.com/l.php?u=https%3A%2F%2Fabout.fb.com%2Fnews%2F2020%2F11%2Fcommunity-standards-enforcement-report-nov-2020%2F&amp;h=AT0fvk2jmPN2Lxdbhn7MhwzMjhAd-tns8xB1nubxBsE4vfgLro6ucrPklXyeYkZvkklurJfDWFTllHGDSgpYmyaAcXgifGNp9FvV71MJDwt_WbqEG0kpj3uhOr7cq-u-19PK30fwZKJWTgz-1sbRr8pxBVBpsWMinJSG" rel="nofollow" target="_blank" data-lynx-mode="asynclazy">enforcement may be limited to circumstances where we have been provided with additional information and context.</a></p><p class="_3i--">People can report potentially violating content, including Pages, Groups, Profiles, individual content, and comments. We also give people control over their own experience by allowing them to <a href="https://www.facebook.com/help/168009843260943?ref=ccs">block</a>, <a href="https://www.facebook.com/help/276458109035418?ref=ccs"> unfollow</a> or <a href="https://www.facebook.com/help/268028706671439?ref=ccs"> hide</a> people and posts. </p><p class="_3i--">The consequences for violating our Community Standards vary depending on the severity of the violation and the person&#039;s history on the platform. For instance, we may warn someone for a first violation, but if they continue to violate our policies, we may restrict their ability to post on Facebook or disable their profile. We also may notify law enforcement when we believe there is a genuine risk of physical harm or a direct threat to public safety.</p><p class="_3i--">Our Community Standards are a guide for what is and isn’t allowed on Facebook. It is in this spirit that we ask members of the Facebook community to follow these guidelines.</p><p class="_3i--"><b> Please note that the US English version of the Community Standards reflects the most up-to-date set of the policies and should be used as the master document.</b></p></div></div></div></div><div class="_2kpl"><div class="_2wqn"><div class="_68lm"><a href="/communitystandards/violence_criminal_behavior/?privacy_mutation_token=eyJ0eXBlIjowLCJjcmVhdGlvbl90aW1lIjoxNjE3MTQ0MzgwLCJjYWxsc2l0ZV9pZCI6Mzg3OTcxMjgyMzgwNTA4fQ%3D%3D"><div class="_4ul3"><div class="_4ul5"><div class="_2wqm"><div class="_2wqo">I.</div>Violence and Criminal Behavior</div></div><div class="_4ul1"><i class="img sp_zy9lX_X4JVW sx_a4441f"></i></div></div></a></div></div><div class="_2wqn"><div class="_68lm"><a href="/communitystandards/safety/?privacy_mutation_token=eyJ0eXBlIjowLCJjcmVhdGlvbl90aW1lIjoxNjE3MTQ0MzgwLCJjYWxsc2l0ZV9pZCI6Mzg3OTcxMjgyMzgwNTA4fQ%3D%3D"><div class="_4ul3"><div class="_4ul5"><div class="_2wqm"><div class="_2wqo">II.</div>Safety</div></div><div class="_4ul1"><i class="img sp_zy9lX_X4JVW sx_a4441f"></i></div></div></a></div></div><div class="_4ul5"><div class="_2wqm"><div class="_2wqo">III.</div>Objectionable Content</div></div><div class="_4ul1"><i class="img sp_zy9lX_X4JVW sx_a4441f"></i></div></div></a></div></div><div While we understand that people commonly express disdain or disagreement by threatening or calling for violence in non-serious ways, we remove language that incites or facilitates serious violence. We remove content, disable accounts, and work with law enforcement when we believe there is a genuine risk of physical harm or direct threats to public safety. We also try to consider the language and context in order to distinguish casual statements from content that constitutes a credible threat to public or personal safety. In determining whether a threat is credible, we may also consider additional information like a person's public visibility and the risks to their physical safety. \n  \n     In some cases, we see We regularly consult with experts in suicide and self-injury to help inform our policies and enforcement, and work with organizations around the world to provide assistance to people in distress.\n     \nWhile we don’t allow people to intentionally or unintentionally celebrate or promote suicide or self-injury, we do allow people to discuss these topics because we want Facebook to be a space where people can share their experiences, raise awareness about these issues, and seek support from one another.\n  \nWe define self-injury as the intentional and direct injuring of the body, including self-mutilation and eating disorders. We remove any content that encourages suicide or self-injury, including fictional content such as memes or illustrations and any self-injury content which is graphic, regardless of context. We also remove content that identifies and negatively targets victims or survivors of suicide or self-injury seriously, humorously or rhetorically, as well as real time depictions of suicide or self-injury. Content about recovery of suicide or self-harm that is allowed, but may contain imagery that could be upsetting, such as a healed scar, is placed behind a sensitivity screen.\n  \nWhen people post or search for suicide or self-injury- related content, we will direct them to local organizations that can provide support and if someone is at immediate risk of harming themselves, we will contact local emergency services to get them help.\n  \nWith respect to live content, experts have told us that if someone is saying they intend to attempt suicide on a livestream, we should leave the content up for as long as possible, because the longer someone is talking to a camera, the more opportunity there is for a friend or family member to call emergency services.\n  \nHowever, to minimize the risk of others being negatively impacted by viewing this content, we will stop the livestream at the point at which the threat turns into an attempt. As mentioned above, in any case, we will contact emergency services if we identify someone is at immediate risk of harming themselves.\n  \n     \n \n We do not tolerate this kind of behavior because it prevents people from feeling safe and respected on Facebook.  \n\n We distinguish between public figures and private individuals because we want to allow discussion, which often includes critical commentary of people who are featured in the news or who have a large public audience. For public figures, we remove attacks that are severe as well as certain attacks where the public figure is directly tagged in the post or comment. For private individuals, our protection goes further: we remove content that's meant to degrade or shame, including, for example, claims about someone's sexual activity. We recognize that bullying and harassment can have more of an emotional impact on minors, which is why our policies provide heightened protection for users between the ages of 13 and 18. \n\n Context and intent matter, and we allow people to post and share if it is clear that something was shared in order to condemn or draw attention to bullying and harassment. In certain instances, we require self-reporting because it helps us understand that the person targeted feels bullied or harassed. Experts think and talk about these issues under one umbrella — human exploitation.   \n     \n     \n     \n      In an effort to disrupt and prevent harm, we remove content that facilitates or coordinates the exploitation of humans, including human trafficking. We define human trafficking as the business of depriving someone of liberty for profit. It is the exploitation of humans in order to force them to engage   in commercial sex, labor, or other activities against their will. It relies on deception, force and coercion, and degrades humans by depriving them of their freedom while economically or materially benefiting others.   \n     \n     \n     \n      Human trafficking is multi-faceted and global; it can affect anyone regardless of age, socioeconomic background, ethnicity, gender, or location. It takes many forms, and any given trafficking situation can involve various stages of development. By the coercive nature of this abuse, victims cannot consent. \n     \n     \n     \n      While we need to be careful not to conflate human trafficking and smuggling, the two can be related and exhibit overlap. The United Nations defines human smuggling as the procurement or facilitation of illegal entry into a state across international borders. Without necessity for coercion or force, it may still result in the exploitation of vulnerable individuals who are trying to leave their country of origin, often in pursuit of a better life. Human smuggling is a crime against a state, relying on movement, and human trafficking is a crime against a person, relying on exploitation. \n \n "},privacy_violations_image_rights:{other_content:"\n freely when they don’t feel attacked on the basis of who they are. That’s why we don’t allow hate speech on Facebook. It creates an environment of intimidation and exclusion, and in some cases may promote offline violence. \n\n     We define hate speech as a direct attack against people on the basis of what we call protected characteristics: race, ethnicity, national origin, disability, religious affiliation, caste, sexual orientation, sex, gender identity and serious disease.  We define attacks as violent or dehumanizing speech, harmful stereotypes, statements of inferiority, expressions of contempt, disgust or dismissal, cursing, and calls for exclusion or segregation. We consider age a protected characteristic when referenced along with another protected characteristic. We also protect refugees, migrants, immigrants and asylum seekers from the most severe attacks, though we do allow commentary and criticism of immigration policies. Similarly, we provide some protections for characteristics like occupation, when they’re referenced along with a protected characteristic. \n    \n    \n     We recognize that people sometimes share content that includes someone else’s hate speech to condemn it or raise awareness. In other cases, speech that might otherwise violate our standards can be used self-referentially or in an empowering way. Our policies are designed to allow room for these types of speech, but we require people to clearly indicate their intent. If intention is unclear, we may remove content. \n    \n\n     Learn more about our approach to hate speech.\n   \n \n "},graphic_violence:{other_content:"\n   \n  \n    Do not post: \n    \n      Imagery of People   \n Videos of people or dead bodies in non-medical settings if they depict\n   \n  \t Dismemberment \n     Visible internal organs; partially decomposed bodies \n     Charred or burning people unless in the context of cremation or self-immolation when that action is a form of political speech or newsworthy \n     Victims of cannibalism \n     Throat-slitting \n        \n \n      Live streams of capital punishment of a person \n\n     \n    \n  \n   \n      \n  For the following content, we include a warning screen so that people are aware the content may be disturbing. We are a service for more than two billion people to freely express themselves across countries and cultures and in dozens of languages. \n     We recognize how important it is for Facebook to be a place where people feel empowered to communicate, and we take seriously our role in keeping abuse off our service. That’s why we’ve  developed a set of Community Standards  that outline what is and is not allowed on Facebook. Our policies are based on feedback from our community and the advice of experts in fields such as technology, public safety and human rights. To ensure that everyone’s voice is valued, we take great care to craft policies that are inclusive of different views and beliefs, in particular those of people and communities that might otherwise be overlooked or marginalized. \n   \n         \n     REITERATING OUR COMMITMENT TO VOICE \n     The goal of our Community Standards has always been to  create a place for expression and give people a voice . This has not and will not change. Building community and bringing the world closer together depends on people’s ability to share diverse views, experiences, ideas and information. We want people to be able to talk openly about the issues that matter to them, even if some may disagree or find them objectionable. In some cases, we allow content for public awareness which would otherwise go against our Community Standards – if it is newsworthy and in the public interest. We do this only after weighing the public interest value against the risk of harm and we look to international human rights standards,  as reflected in our Corporate Human Rights Policy,   to make these judgments. As such, we consider the newsworthiness of content posted by anyone, including news organizations and individuals users. For example, we have allowed content that graphically depicts war or the consequences of war where it is important to public discourse.  \n    \n     Our commitment to expression is paramount, but we recognize the internet creates new and increased opportunities for abuse. For these reasons, when we limit expression, we do it in service of one or more of the following values: \n   \n       \n\n     Authenticity:  We want to make sure the content people are seeing on Facebook is authentic. We believe that authenticity creates a better environment for sharing, and that’s why we don’t want people using Facebook to misrepresent who they are or what they’re doing.\n \n    \n    \n      \n    \n     Safety:  We are committed to making Facebook a safe place. Expression that threatens people has the potential to intimidate, exclude or silence others and isn’t allowed on Facebook. \n  \n    \n  \n    \n    \n     Privacy:  We are committed to protecting personal privacy and information. Privacy gives people the freedom to be themselves, and to choose how and when to share on Facebook and to connect more easily.\n \n        \n  \n    \n     Dignity:  We believe that all people are equal in dignity and rights. We expect that people will respect the dignity of others and not harass or degrade others. \n    \n\n\n    \n    \n     Our Community Standards apply to everyone, all around the world, and to all types of content. They’re designed to be comprehensive – for example, content that might not be considered hateful may still be removed for violating a different policy. We recognize that words mean different things or affect people differently depending on their local community, language, or background. We work hard to account for these nuances while also applying our policies consistently and fairly to people and their expression. Our enforcement of these standards relies on information available to us. In some cases, this means that we may not detect content and behavior that violates these standards, and in others,  enforcement may be limited to circumstances where we have been provided with additional information and context. \n\n     People can report potentially violating content, including Pages, Groups, Profiles, individual content, and comments. We also give people control over their own experience by allowing them to\n       block ,   unfollow \n       or \n        hide  people and posts.\n       \n\n     The consequences for violating our Community Standards vary depending on the severity of the violation and the person's history on the platform. For instance, we may warn someone for a first violation, but if they continue to violate our policies, we may restrict their ability to post on Facebook or disable their profile. We also may notify law enforcement when we believe there is a genuine risk of physical harm or a direct threat to public safety. \n     Our Community Standards are a guide for what is and isn’t allowed on Facebook. It is in this spirit that we ask members of the Facebook community to follow these guidelines. \n     \nPlease note that the US English version of the Community Standards reflects the most up-to-date suic\u00eddio ou de uma tentativa de suic\u00eddio. Tentamos identificar bilhetes de suic\u00eddio usando diversos fatores, incluindo, entre outros, solicita\u00e7\u00f5es de familiares ou representantes legais, not\u00edcias da m\u00eddia, registros policiais ou outras fontes de terceiros (por exemplo, ag\u00eancias do governo e ONGs). \n    \n  \n ","policy_rationale":"\n   N\u00f3s nos preocupamos profundamente com a seguran\u00e7a das pessoas que usam os nossos aplicativos. Consultamos regularmente especialistas em suic\u00eddio e automutila\u00e7\u00e3o para ajudar na cria\u00e7\u00e3o das nossas pol\u00edticas e na aplica\u00e7\u00e3o delas. Al\u00e9m disso, trabalhamos com organiza\u00e7\u00f5es de todo o mundo para fornecer assist\u00eancia a pessoas que estejam em sofrimento psicol\u00f3gico.\n     \nEmbora n\u00e3o permitamos que as pessoas, intencionalmente ou n\u00e3o, comemorem ou promovam o suic\u00eddio ou a automutila\u00e7\u00e3o, permitimos que as pessoas discutam sobre esses t\u00f3picos. Queremos que o Facebook seja um espa\u00e7o onde as pessoas possam compartilhar suas experi\u00eancias, aumentar a conscientiza\u00e7\u00e3o sobre esses problemas e buscar o apoio umas das outras.\n  \nDefinimos a automutila\u00e7\u00e3o como uma agress\u00e3o intencional e direta ao corpo, inclusive dist\u00farbios alimentares. Removemos qualquer conte\u00fado que incentive o suic\u00eddio ou a automutila\u00e7\u00e3o, incluindo conte\u00fado fict\u00edcio, como memes ou ilustra\u00e7\u00f5es, e qualquer conte\u00fado de automutila\u00e7\u00e3o que seja expl\u00edcito, independentemente do contexto. Tamb\u00e9m removemos conte\u00fados que identificam e atacam negativamente v\u00edtimas ou sobreviventes de suic\u00eddio ou automutila\u00e7\u00e3o de forma s\u00e9ria, humor\u00edstica ou ret\u00f3rica, bem como representa\u00e7\u00f5es em tempo real de suic\u00eddio ou de automutila\u00e7\u00e3o. Conte\u00fados sobre a recupera\u00e7\u00e3o de uma tentativa de suic\u00eddio ou de automutila\u00e7\u00e3o que s\u00e3o permitidos mas cont\u00e9m imagens que podem ser perturbadoras, como uma cicatriz curada, s\u00e3o colocados atr\u00e1s de uma tela de sensibilidade.\n  \nQuando algu\u00e9m publicar ou procurar conte\u00fado relacionado a suic\u00eddio ou automutila\u00e7\u00e3o, n\u00f3s direcionaremos essa pessoa para organiza\u00e7\u00f5es locais que podem ajudar. N\u00e3o toleramos este tipo de comportamento porque ele impede que as pessoas se sintam seguras e respeitadas no Facebook.  \n\n Fazemos a distin\u00e7\u00e3o entre figuras p\u00fablicas e indiv\u00edduos privados, pois queremos permitir a discuss\u00e3o, o que inclui com frequ\u00eancia coment\u00e1rios cr\u00edticos de pessoas que s\u00e3o noticiadas na m\u00eddia ou t\u00eam um amplo p\u00fablico. No caso de figuras p\u00fablicas, removemos ataques graves, bem como certos ataques em que elas s\u00e3o marcadas diretamente na publica\u00e7\u00e3o ou no coment\u00e1rio. Para indiv\u00edduos privados, nossa prote\u00e7\u00e3o vai al\u00e9m: removemos conte\u00fado publicado com o objetivo de degradar ou constranger, como alega\u00e7\u00f5es sobre a atividade sexual de algu\u00e9m. Entendemos que o bullying e o ass\u00e9dio podem ter um impacto emocional maior em menores de idade. Por isso, nossas pol\u00edticas oferecem prote\u00e7\u00e3o intensificada aos usu\u00e1rios com idades entre 13 e 18 anos. \n\n O contexto e a inten\u00e7\u00e3o contam. Assim, permitimos que as pessoas postem publica\u00e7\u00f5es se ficar claro que algo foi compartilhado a fim de condenar ou chamar aten\u00e7\u00e3o para o bullying e o ass\u00e9dio. Em certas inst\u00e2ncias, exige-se uma den\u00fancia, porque isso nos ajuda a entender que a pessoa visada sente que \u00e9 v\u00edtima de bullying ou ass\u00e9dio. Al\u00e9m de denunciar o referido comportamento e conte\u00fado, incentivamos as pessoas a usar as  ferramentas dispon\u00edveis no Facebook  para ajudar na prote\u00e7\u00e3o contra tal pr\u00e1tica. \n    \n     Tamb\u00e9m temos uma  Central de Preven\u00e7\u00e3o ao Bullying , que \u00e9 um recurso voltado para adolescentes, pais e educadores em busca de apoio para quest\u00f5es relacionadas ao bullying e a outros conflitos. Ela oferece orienta\u00e7\u00e3o passo a passo, incluindo informa\u00e7\u00f5es sobre como come\u00e7ar conversas sobre bullying. contrabando humano. \n      \n         \n    \n ","policy_rationale":"\n   Com o objetivo de abranger uma ampla gama de atividades prejudiciais que podem se manifestar em nossa plataforma e, ap\u00f3s consultarmos especialistas externos do mundo todo, estamos reunindo diversas pol\u00edticas existentes voltadas para coibir a explora\u00e7\u00e3o humana, que antes estavam espalhadas em diferentes se\u00e7\u00f5es dos Padr\u00f5es da Comunidade, em uma \u00fanica se\u00e7\u00e3o dedicada \u00e0 explora\u00e7\u00e3o humana. Os especialistas se referem a esse tema e o enquadram sob uma \u00fanica categoria: explora\u00e7\u00e3o humana.   \n     \n     \n     \n      Em um esfor\u00e7o para evitar e acabar com danos, removemos conte\u00fado que facilite ou coordene a explora\u00e7\u00e3o humana, incluindo tr\u00e1fico de pessoas. Definimos tr\u00e1fico humano como qualquer atividade que prive uma pessoa de sua liberdade para obten\u00e7\u00e3o de lucro. Tais atividades podem incluir trabalho for\u00e7ado, explora\u00e7\u00e3o sexual comercial   ou qualquer outra pr\u00e1tica imposta contra a vontade de uma pessoa. Elas se valem do engano, da for\u00e7a e da coer\u00e7\u00e3o, e degradam os seres humanos ao priv\u00e1-los de sua liberdade, beneficiando econ\u00f4mica ou materialmente quem as pratica.   \n     \n     \n     \n      O tr\u00e1fico de pessoas \u00e9 multifacetado e global. Ele pode afetar qualquer pessoa, independentemente de sua idade, n\u00edvel socioecon\u00f4mico, etnia, g\u00eanero ou localiza\u00e7\u00e3o. Ele assume v\u00e1rias formas e pode envolver v\u00e1rios est\u00e1gios de desenvolvimento em diversas categorias. Pela natureza coercitiva desse abuso, as v\u00edtimas n\u00e3o podem consentir. \n     \n     \n     \n      Embora tenhamos cuidado para n\u00e3o confundir tr\u00e1fico com contrabando humano, os dois podem estar relacionados e apresentar sobreposi\u00e7\u00f5es. As Na\u00e7\u00f5es Unidas definem o contrabando humano como a contrata\u00e7\u00e3o ou facilita\u00e7\u00e3o da entrada ilegal em um Estado atravessando fronteiras internacionais. Ainda que a pr\u00e1tica n\u00e3o se valha de coer\u00e7\u00e3o ou for\u00e7a, ela ainda pode resultar na explora\u00e7\u00e3o de indiv\u00edduos vulner\u00e1veis que est\u00e3o tentando deixar seu pa\u00eds de origem, geralmente em busca de uma vida melhor. O contrabando humano \u00e9 um crime contra um Estado, de car\u00e1ter transnacional; j\u00e1 o tr\u00e1fico humano \u00e9 um crime contra uma pessoa, com o objetivo de explor\u00e1-la. \n \n  \n ","policy_rationale":"\n   Acreditamos que as pessoas se comunicam e se conectam mais livremente quando n\u00e3o se sentem atacadas pelo que s\u00e3o. \u00c9 por isso que n\u00e3o permitimos discursos de \u00f3dio no Facebook. Isso cria um ambiente de intimida\u00e7\u00e3o e exclus\u00e3o que, em alguns casos, pode promover a viol\u00eancia no mundo real. \n\n     Definimos discurso de \u00f3dio como um ataque direto a pessoas baseado no que chamamos de caracter\u00edsticas protegidas: ra\u00e7a, etnia, nacionalidade, religi\u00e3o orienta\u00e7\u00e3o sexual, casta, sexo, g\u00eanero, identidade de g\u00eanero e doen\u00e7a grave ou defici\u00eancia. Definimos ataques como discursos violentos ou degradantes, estere\u00f3tipos prejudiciais, declara\u00e7\u00f5es de inferioridade, express\u00f5es de desprezo, repugn\u00e2ncia ou rejei\u00e7\u00e3o, xingamentos e apelos \u00e0 exclus\u00e3o ou segrega\u00e7\u00e3o. Consideramos a idade uma caracter\u00edstica protegida quando referenciada juntamente com outra caracter\u00edstica tamb\u00e9m protegida. Tamb\u00e9m protegemos refugiados, migrantes, imigrantes e pessoas que buscam asilo de ataques mais severos, embora permitamos coment\u00e1rios e cr\u00edticas \u00e0s pol\u00edticas de imigra\u00e7\u00e3o. Da mesma forma, fornecemos algumas prote\u00e7\u00f5es para aspectos como ocupa\u00e7\u00e3o, quando estes s\u00e3o mencionados juntamente com uma caracter\u00edstica protegida. \n    \n    \n     Reconhecemos que as pessoas \u00e0s vezes compartilham conte\u00fados que incluem discursos de \u00f3dio de outra pessoa para conden\u00e1-la ou aumentar a conscientiza\u00e7\u00e3o. Em outros casos, o discurso que poderia violar nossas normas pode ser usado de forma autorreferencial ou empoderadora. Nossas pol\u00edticas visam dar espa\u00e7o para estes tipos de discurso, mas exigimos que as pessoas indiquem claramente sua inten\u00e7\u00e3o. Se a inten\u00e7\u00e3o n\u00e3o estiver clara, poderemos remover o conte\u00fado. \n    \n\n     Saiba mais sobre nossa vis\u00e3o sobre discurso de \u00f3dio.   \n \n "},"graphic_violence":{"other_content":"\n   \n  \n    N\u00e3o publique: \n    \n      Imagens de pessoas   \n V\u00eddeos de pessoas ou cad\u00e1veres em instala\u00e7\u00f5es n\u00e3o m\u00e9dicas se retratarem:\n   \n  \t Desmembramento \n     \u00d3rg\u00e3os internos vis\u00edveis; corpos parcialmente decompostos \n     Pessoas queimadas ou carbonizadas, exceto no contexto de crema\u00e7\u00e3o ou autoimola\u00e7\u00e3o como forma de discurso pol\u00edtico ou como algo digno de not\u00edcia \n     V\u00edtimas de canibalismo \n     Corte de garganta \n        \n \n      Streams ao vivo da pena de morte de uma pessoa \n\n     \n    \n  \n   \n      \n  Para o conte\u00fado a seguir, inclu\u00edmos uma tela de aviso para alertar as pessoas de que o conte\u00fado pode ser perturbador. Nossas pol\u00edticas s\u00e3o baseadas no feedback de nossa comunidade e nos conselhos de especialistas de algumas \u00e1reas, como tecnologia, seguran\u00e7a p\u00fablica e direitos humanos. Isso n\u00e3o mudou e n\u00e3o mudar\u00e1. Criar uma comunidade e unir pessoas depende da capacidade de compartilhar diversos pontos de vista, experi\u00eancias, ideias e informa\u00e7\u00f5es. Queremos que as pessoas possam falar abertamente sobre os assuntos importantes para elas, ainda que sejam temas que geram controv\u00e9rsias e obje\u00e7\u00f5es. Em alguns casos, permitimos conte\u00fado que poderia ir contra os nossos Padr\u00f5es da Comunidade para fins de conscientiza\u00e7\u00e3o p\u00fablica, caso ele seja interessante e de utilidade p\u00fablica. Para fazer esses julgamentos, consideramos o valor do interesse p\u00fablico e o risco de dano. Tamb\u00e9m observamos os padr\u00f5es internacionais relativos a direitos humanos,  como mostrado na nossa Pol\u00edtica Corporativa de Direitos Humanos . Dessa forma, avaliamos a import\u00e2ncia do conte\u00fado publicado por algu\u00e9m, incluindo organiza\u00e7\u00f5es de not\u00edcias e usu\u00e1rios individuais. Acreditamos que a autenticidade cria um ambiente melhor para o compartilhamento, e \u00e9 por isso que n\u00e3o queremos que as pessoas usem o Facebook para falsificar a pr\u00f3pria identidade ou o que est\u00e3o fazendo.\n \n    \n    \n      \n    \n     Seguran\u00e7a:  temos o compromisso de fazer com que o Facebook seja um lugar seguro. A privacidade d\u00e1 \u00e0s pessoas a liberdade de ser quem elas realmente s\u00e3o, escolher como e quando compartilhar no Facebook e criar conex\u00f5es mais facilmente.\n \n        \n  \n    \n     Dignidade:  acreditamos que todas as pessoas s\u00e3o iguais no que diz respeito \u00e0 dignidade e a direitos. Esperamos que as pessoas respeitem a dignidade alheia e n\u00e3o assediem ou difamem terceiros. \n    \n\n\n    \n    \n     Nossos Padr\u00f5es da Comunidade se aplicam a todos, no mundo inteiro, e a todos os tipos de conte\u00fado. Eles foram concebidos para que fossem abrangentes. Por exemplo, o conte\u00fado que talvez n\u00e3o seja considerado discurso de \u00f3dio ainda pode ser removido por viola\u00e7\u00e3o de uma pol\u00edtica diferente. Reconhecemos que as palavras t\u00eam diferentes significados ou afetam as pessoas de maneiras diversas dependendo da comunidade local, idioma ou origem. Trabalhamos com muito empenho para levar essas nuances em considera\u00e7\u00e3o e procuramos aplicar nossas pol\u00edticas de forma consistente e justa \u00e0s pessoas e express\u00f5es individuais. Nossa aplica\u00e7\u00e3o desses padr\u00f5es depende das informa\u00e7\u00f5es dispon\u00edveis para n\u00f3s. Em alguns casos, podemos n\u00e3o detectar conte\u00fado e comportamento que violem esses padr\u00f5es e, em outros,  a aplica\u00e7\u00e3o pode estar limitada \u00e0s circunst\u00e2ncias em que nos forneceram informa\u00e7\u00f5es e contexto adicionais. \n\n     As pessoas podem denunciar conte\u00fado com potencial de viola\u00e7\u00e3o, incluindo P\u00e1ginas, grupos, perfis, conte\u00fado individual e coment\u00e1rios.
